# Text Elements
Phenols ^bNlLMKhX

Production of Phenol ^FidCg892

Step 3 - Forming the Diazonium Salt ^Wvcehw0Y

Nitrous Acid ^SK6NdTec

Step 1 - Forming HNO2 ^dMwdsV91

Step 2 - Diazonium Salt ^mNr69IUH

Benzenediazonium
Chloride ^OHVl4KkQ

Phenylamine ^LngkXC7k

Unstable
Diazonium Salt ^ORj4osCR

Bases ^XKDUZQqS

Bromination ^oUXPTuSr

Diazonium Salts ^CUuyWqn3

Nitration ^t0h8E7Ug

Reactive Metals ^anOQxeHC

Bromination ^7LEc2pCA

Sodium
Phenoxide ^WQBy3KRd

Phenols are only slightly soluble in water due to the large non-polar benzene
 ring
However, they do dissolve in alkaline solutions and undergo acid-base
reactions with bases to form a soluble salt and water ^fzgPvhHp

Acid Base reactions ^sh658mXz

Molten phenols react vigorously with reactive metals such
as sodium (Na)
This is also an acid-base reaction
Now, a soluble salt is formed and hydrogen gas is given off ^p2kI5avk

Bases ^HoVbRODY

Acid Base reactions ^7R6e0GTX

Room
Temp ^52Vr7OuA

Phenols also undergo electrophilic substitution reactionswhen reacted with
bromine water at room temperature
Phenol decolourises the orange bromine solution to form a white precipitate
 of 2,4,6-tribromophenol
This is also known as the bromination of phenol
 ^yRAmpHL3

Reactive Metals ^n52TqXsk

Orange
Solution ^KO62J4DH

2,4,6 Tribromo-
phenol (White
perticipate) ^cN5szlRI

Step 2 ^FClKVV7v

Step 1 ^dpm1N4yq

Sodium
Phenoxide ^wmQKZhwZ

Azo Compound
(Yellow-Orange Perticipate) ^SDjzgX3S

Benzene
Diazonium ion ^LtBcYAsv

Phenoxide Ion ^MqXqwvAB

Diazonium ions are very reactive compounds containing an -N2+ group
When phenols are dissolved in sodium hydroxide (NaOH), a solution of sodium phenoxide is 
obtained
This solution is cooled in ice and cold diazonium ion is added to the sodium phenoxide
After the reaction has occurred, a yellow-orange solution or precipitate of an azo compound is 
formed
These are compounds in which two benzene rings are linked by a nitrogen bridge ^SPslKeq4
